class="vector-column-end">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class="vector-sticky-pinned-container">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<nav class="vector-page-tools-landmark" aria-label="Page tools">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="vector-page-tools-pinned-container" class="vector-pinned-container">\n\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</nav>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<nav class="vector-appearance-landmark" aria-label="Appearance">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="vector-appearance-pinned-container" class="vector-pinned-container">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="vector-appearance" class="vector-appearance vector-pinnable-element">\n\t<div\n\tclass="vector-pinnable-header vector-appearance-pinnable-header data-event-name="pinnable-header.vector-appearance.unpin">hide</button>\n</div>\n\n\n</div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</nav>\n\t\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body" aria-labelledby="firstHeading" data-mw-ve-target-container>\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class="vector-body-before-content">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class="mw-indicators">\n\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lechon&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Lechon">Lechon</a>)</span></div></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Piglet fed on its mother\'s milk</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:St_John_Restaurant,_Smithfield,_London_(4410621202).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/St_John_Restaurant%2C_Smithfield%2C_London_%284410621202%29.jpg/225px-St_John_Restaurant%2C_Smithfield%2C_London_%284410621202%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="225" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/St_John_Restaurant%2C_Smithfield%2C_London_%284410621202%29.jpg/338px-St_John_Restaurant%2C_Smithfield%2C_London_%284410621202%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/St_John_Restaurant%2C_Smithfield%2C_London_%284410621202%29.jpg/450px-St_John_Restaurant%2C_Smithfield%2C_London_%284410621202%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2418" data-file-height="1612" /></a><figcaption>A suckling pig prepared at St. John Restaurant, London</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cochinillo.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Cochinillo.jpg/225px-Cochinillo.jpg" decoding="async" width="225" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Cochinillo.jpg/338px-Cochinillo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Cochinillo.jpg/450px-Cochinillo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2205" data-file-height="1470" /></a><figcaption>Suckling pig being grilled at La Paloma fair in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, among ribs and other pork produce</figcaption></figure>\n<p>A <b>suckling pig</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Piglet_(animal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Piglet (animal)">piglet</a> fed on its <a href="/wiki/Pig_milk" title="Pig milk">mother\'s milk</a> (i.e., a piglet which is still a "<a href="/wiki/Suckling" class="mw-redirect" title="Suckling">suckling</a>"). In <a href="/wiki/Culinary" class="mw-redirect" title="Culinary">culinary</a> contexts, a suckling pig is <a href="/wiki/Animal_slaughter" title="Animal slaughter">slaughtered</a> between the ages of two and six weeks. It is traditionally cooked whole, often <a href="/wiki/Roasting" title="Roasting">roasted</a>, in various cuisines. It is usually prepared for special occasions and gatherings. The most popular preparation can be found in Spain and Portugal under the name <i><b>lech\xc3\xb3n</b></i> (Spanish) or <i><b>leit\xc3\xa3o</b></i> (Portuguese).\n</p><p>The meat from suckling pig is pale and tender and the cooked skin is crisp and can be used for <a href="/wiki/Pork_rinds" class="mw-redirect" title="Pork rinds">pork rinds</a>. The texture of the meat can be somewhat gelatinous due to the amount of <a href="/wiki/Collagen" title="Collagen">collagen</a> in a young pig.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are many ancient recipes for suckling pig from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Roman_cuisine" title="Ancient Roman cuisine">Roman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">Chinese cuisine</a>. Since the pig is one of the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_domesticated_animals" title="List of domesticated animals">animals domesticated</a> by human beings for slaughter, many references to pigs are found in human culture. The suckling pig, specifically, appears in early texts such as the sixth-century <a href="/wiki/Salic_law" title="Salic law">Salic law</a>. As an example of a law governing the punishment for theft, Title 2, article 1, is, in Latin, <span title="Medieval Latin-language text"><i lang="la">Si quis porcellum lactantem furaverit, et ei fuerit adprobatum (malb. chrane calcium hoc est) CXX dinarios qui faciunt solidos III culpabilis iudicetur</i></span>. "If someone has stolen a suckling pig and this is proven against him, the guilty party will be sentenced to 120 <a href="/wiki/Denarius" title="Denarius">denarii</a> which adds up to three <a href="/wiki/Solidus_(coin)" title="Solidus (coin)">solidi</a> (Latin coins)." The words <span title="Old Frankish-language text"><i lang="frk">chrane calcium</i></span> are written in Frankish; <span title="Old Frankish-language text"><i lang="frk">calcium</i></span> (or <span title="Old Frankish-language text"><i lang="frk">galza</i></span> in other manuscripts) is the <a href="/wiki/Gloss_(annotation)#In_linguistics" title="Gloss (annotation)">gloss</a> for "suckling pig"; <span title="Medieval Latin-language text"><i lang="la">porcellum lactantem</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These glosses in Frankish, the so-called <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malbergse_Glossen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Malbergse Glossen (page does not exist)">Malbergse Glossen</a></i>, are considered the earliest attested words in <a href="/wiki/Old_Dutch" title="Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Regional_dishes">Regional dishes</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Regional dishes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are various preparations for suckling pig in Western and Asian cuisines.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Latin_countries">Latin countries</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Latin countries"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1235681985">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px class="side-box-image"><span class="noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg/40px-Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg/60px-Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg/80px-Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="400" /></span></span></div>\n<div class="side-box-text plainlist">Wikibooks <a href="https://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/Cookbook" class="extiw" title="wikibooks:Cookbook">Cookbook</a> has a recipe/module on\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409"><div class="plainlist" style="margin-left: 1.6em;">\n<ul><li><i><b><a href="https://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/Cookbook:Lechon_asado" class="extiw" title="wikibooks:Cookbook:Lechon asado"> Lechon asado</a></b></i></li></ul>\n</div></div></div>\n</div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Lechazo" title="Lechazo">Lechazo</a>.</div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cochinillo_asado" title="Cochinillo asado">Cochinillo asado</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Lech%C3%B3n_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Lech\xc3\xb3n (disambiguation)">Lech\xc3\xb3n (disambiguation)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leit%C3%A3o_(disambiguation)" title="Leit\xc3\xa3o (disambiguation)">Leit\xc3\xa3o (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cochinillo_asado-Madrid.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Cochinillo_asado-Madrid.jpg/220px-Cochinillo_asado-Madrid.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Cochinillo_asado-Madrid.jpg/330px-Cochinillo_asado-Madrid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Cochinillo_asado-Madrid.jpg/440px-Cochinillo_asado-Madrid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>Spanish <i><a href="/wiki/Cochinillo_asado" title="Cochinillo asado">cochinillo asado</a></i></figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Porcetto_sardo_3.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Porcetto_sardo_3.jpg/220px-Porcetto_sardo_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Porcetto_sardo_3.jpg/330px-Porcetto_sardo_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Porcetto_sardo_3.jpg/440px-Porcetto_sardo_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2400" /></a><figcaption><i>Su porcheddu</i>, <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Sardinian cuisine">Sardinian cuisine</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p><i><b>Lech\xc3\xb3n</b></i> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;le\xcb\x88t\xca\x83on&#93;</a></span>; from <i>leche</i> "milk" + -\xc3\xb3n), <i><b>cochinillo asado</b></i> (Spanish, literally "roasted suckling pig"), or <i><b>leit\xc3\xa3o</b></i> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>; from <i>leite</i> "milk" + -\xc3\xa3o) is a pork dish in several regions of the world, most specifically in <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Spain">Spain</a> (in particular <a href="/wiki/Segovia" title="Segovia">Segovia</a>), <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> (in particular <a href="/wiki/Bairrada" class="mw-redirect" title="Bairrada">Bairrada</a>) and regions worldwide previously colonized by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> or <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>. <i>Lech\xc3\xb3n/Leit\xc3\xa3o</i> is a word referring to a <a href="/wiki/Roasted" class="mw-redirect" title="Roasted">roasted</a> baby pig (piglet) which was still fed by <a href="/wiki/Breastfeeding" title="Breastfeeding">suckling</a> its mother\'s milk (a suckling pig). Lech\xc3\xb3n/Leit\xc3\xa3o is a popular item in the cuisine in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> (in the United States), Spain, Cuba, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, Honduras, Argentina, Uruguay, Bolivia, Ecuador, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, Costa Rica, the Dominican Republic, and other <a href="/wiki/Hispanidad" title="Hispanidad">Spanish-speaking nations</a> in Latin America, as well as in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and other Portuguese-speaking nations.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is also present as <i><b>cochon de lait</b></i> in the French-Swiss and <a href="/wiki/French_cuisine" title="French cuisine">French</a> cuisines (in particular in <a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">Metz</a>), in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> (in particular in <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Sardinian cuisine">Sardinian cuisine</a> as <i><b>su porcheddu</b></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Langenfeld_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Langenfeld-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The dish features a whole roasted suckling <a href="/wiki/Pig" title="Pig">pig</a> cooked over <a href="/wiki/Charcoal" title="Charcoal">charcoal</a>. It has been described as a national dish of Cuba, Puerto Rico, Spain, Portugal, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. However, the pig-roasting traditions of the Philippines (similar to other <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian</a> regions) have native pre-colonial origins. The meaning of "lechon" in Filipino has diverted from the original Spanish term<sup id="cite_ref-Palanca_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Palanca-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to become a general term for "roasted pig", and is used in reference to adult roasted pigs rather than to suckling pigs, with <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">Cebu</a> being asserted by American chef <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Bourdain" title="Anthony Bourdain">Anthony Bourdain</a> as having the best pigs.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In most of these regions, lech\xc3\xb3n/leit\xc3\xa3o is prepared throughout the year for special occasions, during festivals. It is the centerpiece of the tradition Cuban <a href="/wiki/Christmas_dinner" title="Christmas dinner">Christmas feast</a> <i>La Noche Buena</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After seasoning, the piglet is cooked by skewering the entire animal, entrails removed, on a large stick and cooking it in a pit filled with charcoal. The piglet is placed over the charcoal, and the stick or rod it is attached to is turned in a <a href="/wiki/Rotisserie" title="Rotisserie">rotisserie</a> action.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Colombia">Colombia</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colombia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Colombian_cuisine" title="Colombian cuisine">Colombian cuisine</a></div>\n<p><i><b>Lechona</b></i>, also known as <i>lech\xc3\xb3n asado</i>, is a popular <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombian</a> <a href="/wiki/Recipe" title="Recipe">dish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is similar in style to many preparations made in other <a href="/wiki/South_American" class="mw-redirect" title="South American">South American</a> countries, consisting of a roasted <a href="/wiki/Pig" title="Pig">pig</a> stuffed with <a href="/wiki/Yellow_peas" class="mw-redirect" title="Yellow peas">yellow peas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scallion" title="Scallion">green onion</a>, and spices, cooked in an outdoor brick <a href="/wiki/Oven" title="Oven">oven</a> for several hours. Yellow rice is sometimes added, especially in Bogot\xc3\xa1. It is mostly traditional to the <a href="/wiki/Tolima_Department" title="Tolima Department">Tolima Department</a> in central Colombia and is usually accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Arepa" title="Arepa">arepas</a>, a corn-based dough.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Puerto_Rico">Puerto Rico</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_cuisine" title="Puerto Rican cuisine">Puerto Rican cuisine</a></div>\n<p>The dish has been described as a national dish of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The name of the dish in Puerto Rico is <i>lech\xc3\xb3n asado</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is a traditional dish served at festivals and holidays.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Southeast_Asia">Southeast Asia</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Southeast Asia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Indonesia">Indonesia</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Indonesia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Babi_Guling-Roast_suckling_pig-01.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Babi_Guling-Roast_suckling_pig-01.jpg/220px-Babi_Guling-Roast_suckling_pig-01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Babi_Guling-Roast_suckling_pig-01.jpg/330px-Babi_Guling-Roast_suckling_pig-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Babi_Guling-Roast_suckling_pig-01.jpg/440px-Babi_Guling-Roast_suckling_pig-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Balinese_cuisine" title="Balinese cuisine">Balinese</a> <i>babi guling</i></figcaption></figure>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, roast pig (using both adult or suckling pig) is called <i>babi guling</i>, <i>babi putar</i>, <i>babi panggang</i> or <i>babi bakar</i>; it is predominantly found in non-Muslim majority regions, such as Hindu <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> and Christian <a href="/wiki/Batak_(Indonesia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Batak (Indonesia)">Batak</a> lands in <a href="/wiki/North_Sumatra" title="North Sumatra">North Sumatra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Minahasa" class="mw-redirect" title="Minahasa">Minahasa</a> people of <a href="/wiki/North_Sulawesi" title="North Sulawesi">North Sulawesi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toraja" class="mw-redirect" title="Toraja">Toraja</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Sulawesi" title="South Sulawesi">South Sulawesi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_(province)" title="Papua (province)">Papua</a>, and also among <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesian" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Indonesian">Chinese Indonesians</a>. In Bali, <i>babi guling</i> is usually served with <a href="/wiki/Lawar_(food)" title="Lawar (food)">lawar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steamed_rice" class="mw-redirect" title="Steamed rice">steamed rice</a>; it is a popular dish in Balinese restaurants and <a href="/wiki/Warung" title="Warung">warungs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the Batak people\'s tradition, <i>babi guling</i> is a prerequisite in wedding offerings by the bride\'s family. In Papua, pigs and yams are roasted in heated stones placed in a hole dug in the ground and covered with leaves; this cooking method is called <i>bakar batu</i> (burning the stone), and it is an important cultural and social event among Papuan people.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Philippines">Philippines</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Philippines"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Filipino_lechon" class="mw-redirect" title="Filipino lechon">Filipino lechon</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lechon_Camiguin.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Lechon_Camiguin.jpg/220px-Lechon_Camiguin.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Lechon_Camiguin.jpg/330px-Lechon_Camiguin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Lechon_Camiguin.jpg/440px-Lechon_Camiguin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1183" data-file-height="788" /></a><figcaption><i>Lechon de leche</i> being cooked traditionally in <a href="/wiki/Camiguin" title="Camiguin">Camiguin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, a former Spanish colony, also has a dish that acquired the Spanish name "lech\xc3\xb3n" (usually spelled <i>lechon</i> without <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a>, but also <i>litson</i> or <i>lichon</i>); but it differs from the Spanish lech\xc3\xb3n in that it uses adult pigs, uses different native ingredients (distinctively <a href="/wiki/Lemongrass" class="mw-redirect" title="Lemongrass">lemongrass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Binucao" class="mw-redirect" title="Binucao">binucao</a> fruits, <a href="/wiki/Tamarind" title="Tamarind">tamarind</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a> leaves), is cooked differently, and is pre-colonial in origin (natively known as <i>inasal</i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Inihaw" title="Inihaw">inihaw</a> [na baboy]</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Palanca_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Palanca-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Faicol_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faicol-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is most similar to neighboring native dishes like the <a href="/wiki/Balinese_people" title="Balinese people">Balinese</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Babi_guling" class="mw-redirect" title="Babi guling">babi guling</a></i> (though differing in the stuffing and spices used).<sup id="cite_ref-Paredes_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paredes-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Patawaran_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Patawaran-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Variants of lech\xc3\xb3n that use suckling pigs are differentiated as <i>lechon de leche</i> (which in Spanish would be a linguistic redundancy), but otherwise are cooked in the native way as in regular lechon.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The dish that is explicitly derived from the Spanish lech\xc3\xb3n style of cooking is known as <i>cochinillo</i>. Unlike native Filipino lechons which are stuffed and cooked slowly over charcoals on a bamboo spit, <i>cochinillo</i> uses a suckling pig that is splayed and roasted in an oven.<sup id="cite_ref-Avelis_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avelis-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The term <i>lechon</i> has also become generalized as a <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanword</a> for anything spit-roasted over coals. It is also used for other Filipino dishes like <a href="/wiki/Lechon_manok" title="Lechon manok">lechon manok</a> (native roasted chicken) and <a href="/wiki/Lechon_baka" class="mw-redirect" title="Lechon baka">lechon baka</a> (a whole cow spit-roasted Filipino-style), thus lechon made from whole pig is differentiated as "lechon baboy" (literally "pig lechon").<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reyes_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reyes-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Merano2_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merano2-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="East_Asia">East Asia</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: East Asia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="China">China</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: China"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In various Chinese communities (especially in Southern China), a roast suckling pig is purchased for special family occasions, business launches, or as a ritualistic spiritual offering. For example, one tradition is to offer one or several whole roast suckling pigs to the <a href="/wiki/Jade_Emperor" title="Jade Emperor">Jade Emperor</a> to celebrate a Chinese film\'s opening. The pig is sacrificed to ward off evils and in prayer for the film\'s success. One garnish used to make the dish look more appealing is a circular slice of pineapple and cherry, and is often placed in a red box for luck.\n</p><p>Suckling pig dishes in parts of Southeast Asia, like <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, are also influenced by ethnic Chinese cuisine. Roast suckling pig is eaten in Chinese or Vietnamese restaurants for important parties.<sup id="cite_ref-eastweek_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eastweek-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is also a popular dish at wedding dinners or a party for a baby\'s completion of its first month of life.<sup id="cite_ref-sina_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sina-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rthk_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rthk-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Shaoruzhu.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Cantonese style roasted whole suckling pig"><img alt="Cantonese style roasted whole suckling pig" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Shaoruzhu.jpg/90px-Shaoruzhu.jpg" decoding="async" width="90" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Shaoruzhu.jpg/135px-Shaoruzhu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Shaoruzhu.jpg/180px-Shaoruzhu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">Cantonese style roasted whole suckling pig</div>\n\t\t</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Roast_Suckling_Pig_(2505471024).jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Roast suckling pig bearing \xe5\x9b\x8d (Double Happiness) placard at a Cantonese wedding"><img alt="Roast suckling pig bearing \xe5\x9b\x8d (Double Happiness) placard at a Cantonese wedding" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Roast_Suckling_Pig_%282505471024%29.jpg/120px-Roast_Suckling_Pig_%282505471024%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Roast_Suckling_Pig_%282505471024%29.jpg/180px-Roast_Suckling_Pig_%282505471024%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Roast_Suckling_Pig_%282505471024%29.jpg/240px-Roast_Suckling_Pig_%282505471024%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">Roast suckling pig bearing \xe5\x9b\x8d (<a href="/wiki/Double_Happiness_(calligraphy)" title="Double Happiness (calligraphy)">Double Happiness</a>) placard at a Cantonese wedding</div>\n\t\t</li>\n</ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Northern_Europe">Northern Europe</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Northern Europe"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_cuisine" title="European cuisine">European cuisines</a> of Austria, Croatia, England, Georgia, Germany, Macedonia, the Netherlands, Russia, Serbia, Slovenia, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> and Sweden<sup id="cite_ref-Langenfeld_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Langenfeld-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> favor the dish highly as well. It accompanies <a href="/wiki/Goose" title="Goose">goose</a> as the traditional Christmas feast of families in Russia and Serbia, while the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Navy" title="Russian Navy">Russian Navy</a> maintains a tradition of presenting a roast piglet (or several) to the crew of a ship returning from deployment.\n</p><p>Suckling pig is known in German, Austrian and German-Swiss cuisines as <i><b>Spanferkel</b></i> and in the Dutch cuisine as <i><b>speenvarken</b></i>. It can be roasted in the oven<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or grilled, and is often served at festive occasions such as <a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">Oktoberfest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In Sweden suckling pig is called <i><b>sp\xc3\xa4dgris</b></i>, it is usually cooked in the oven, or sometimes roasted directly over the fire. It is often stuffed with various fruits such as apples and plums, together with butter and breadcrumbs.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Mijo_pe%C4%8De_odojak_-_panoramio.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Odojak na ra\xc5\xbenju, Croatian cuisine"><img alt="Odojak na ra\xc5\xbenju, Croatian cuisine" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Mijo_pe%C4%8De_odojak_-_panoramio.jpg/120px-Mijo_pe%C4%8De_odojak_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Mijo_pe%C4%8De_odojak_-_panoramio.jpg/180px-Mijo_pe%C4%8De_odojak_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Mijo_pe%C4%8De_odojak_-_panoramio.jpg/240px-Mijo_pe%C4%8De_odojak_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext"><i>Odojak na ra\xc5\xbenju</i>, <a href="/wiki/Croatian_cuisine" title="Croatian cuisine">Croatian cuisine</a></div>\n\t\t</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Ganzes_Spanferkel.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Spanferkel, German cuisine"><img alt="Spanferkel, German cuisine" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Ganzes_Spanferkel.jpg/80px-Ganzes_Spanferkel.jpg" decoding="async" width="80" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Ganzes_Spanferkel.jpg/120px-Ganzes_Spanferkel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Ganzes_Spanferkel.jpg/160px-Ganzes_Spanferkel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1513" data-file-height="2270" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext"><i>Spanferkel</i>, <a href="/wiki/German_cuisine" title="German cuisine">German cuisine</a></div>\n\t\t</li>\n</ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="United_States">United States</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suckling_pig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: United States"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The suckling pig is used in <a href="/wiki/Cajun_cuisine" title="Cajun cuisine">Cajun cuisine</a> in the southern U.S., where the <i>Cochon de Lait</i> Festival<sup id="cite_ref-cochondelait_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cochondelait-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is held annually in the small town of <a href="/wiki/Mansura,_Louisiana" title="Mansura, Louisiana">Mansura, Louisiana</a>. During this festival, as its name implies, suckling pigs are roasted. Other uses for the suckling pig in the U.S. include slow roasting in an oven or (as in a Hawaiian-style <a href="/wiki/Pig_roast" title="Pig roast">pig roast</a>) in a pit. The latter remains popular in the <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Southern_United_States" title="Cuisine of the Southern United States">cuisine of the Southern United States</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span
